[1] "The demand for propylene has grown significantly over the years, leading to the development of new production methods, including propane dehydrogenation (PDH)."
          [2] "The PDH process is considered one of the most promising propylene production methods compared to methanol-to-olefins, Fischer-Tropsch-to-olefins, etc."
          [3] "Crucial insights into the PDH process include understanding the adsorption of key propyl intermediates on the catalyst surface."
          [4] "The regulation of material structure and reaction performance at the molecular and atomic levels has attracted extensive attention."
          [5] "The PDH reaction can occur on an individual active site, while larger ensembles of active sites induce structure-sensitive side reactions."
          [6] "To improve the PDH process, strategies involving promoter and support effects have been developed."
          [7] "Catalysts based on metals and/or metal oxides with tunable geometric and electronic properties play crucial roles."
          [8] "The use of promoters such as Cu, Fe, Mn, Co, Sn, Ga, In, Zn can enhance dispersion and tailor electronic states."
          [9] "Supports like Al2O3, SiO2, zeolites can regulate the shape of nanostructured particles and metals-support interaction."
          [10] "Reductive treatment can introduce defects like oxygen vacancies, hydroxyl groups, hydrides enhancing catalytic activity."
          [11] "Promoters like Mg can help disperse V2O5 nanoparticles into polymerized VOx, reducing coke formation."
          [12] "Encapsulation of metal promoters through MSI can alter electron states, affecting catalytic performance."
          [13] "Mesoporous materials provide alternatives for accessing more active sites, confining oxide NPs to prevent sintering."
          [14] "Future challenges include designing NCs with well-defined morphologies and active sites, utilizing in situ/operando techniques."
          [15] "Expanding screening to cheaper transition metals and developing scalable synthesis technologies remains a challenge."
          [16] "CL-ODH as an alternative offers potential, but requires development of nontoxic oxygen carriers with high activity and stability."

[5] "As synthesized CrOx-based catalysts contain multiple oxidation states of Cr, including VI, IV, III, and II, but Cr3+ becomes the main species at reaction conditions."
          [6] "The ability of Ga/H-ZSM-5 to dehydrogenate light alkanes to alkenes was well appreciated."
          [7] "Different Ga species have been proposed to be the active center of the PDH, that is, Ga+, [GaO]+, [Ga(OH)2]+, [GaOH]2+, [GaH]2+, [GaH2]+, and Ga+H+ pair."
          [8] "We combined in situ transmission Fourier-transform infrared (FTIR) spectroscopy, pulse titration studies, and PDH kinetics to demonstrate that the Ga speciation and their PDH performance are dependent on both Ga/Al ratios and Al distributions of the zeolites."
          [9] "Similar to Ga/H-ZSM-5, multiple Zn species have been reported in Zn/H-ZSM-5, that is, isolated Zn2+, isolated [ZnOH]+, multinuclear ZnO clusters, and bulk ZnO aggregates."
          [10] "It was concluded that isolated In+ sites rather than InHx were the stable active site for PDH, which was independent of the Al distribution."

[1] "The increasing propylene demand combined with the use of alternative feedstocks such as shale gas has amplified the pressure towards propene production and the development of light alkane dehydrogenation processes."
          [2] "While the two principal industrial processes for PDH utilize CrAl2O3 (CATOFIN) and PtSnAl2O3 (Oleflex) supported catalysts, other materials such as gallium-based catalysts are receiving considerable attention as alternative catalysts."
          [3] "Gallium-based zeolites have already been implemented for the conversion of lightweight alkanes to aromatics and H2, a process proposed to involve a tandem dehydrogenation aromatization process."
          [4] "Ga2O3 and related materials have also been investigated as catalysts for alkane conversion, specifically PDH due to the high selectivity for propylene."
          [5] "Several computational and experimental studies have aimed at identifying these active sites,4f, 4h, 4i, 7 which so far remains a topic of debate."
          [6] "Silica-supported gallium species have been recently prepared by electrostatic adsorption methods.7a While showing promising results, the structure of the active sites is unknown."
          [7] "Surface organometallic chemistry (SOMC) allows for the generation of well-defined surface species on a variety of supports via grafting of tailored molecular precursors on supports with isolated OH sites.8 Thus, we reasoned that the development of an appropriate molecular precursor would allow for generating well-defined isolated active sites of gallium outside of bulk Ga2O3."
          [8] "A two-step approach, involving both SOMC and the thermolytic molecular precursor approach has previously been implemented to generate isolated surface sites with controlled oxidation state and nuclearity.9 Herein we describe the synthesis, structural characterization of the molecular complex [Ga(OSi(OtBu)3)3(THF)] (1)10 and its utilization as a precursor for generating gallium single-sites on silica."
          [9] "These isolated gallium sites were achieved through grafting of 1 on silica followed by a thermolysis step at 500 C under high vacuum."
          [10] "The presented gallium species display unprecedented catalytic performances, combining high activity, selectivity and stability in the dehydrogenation of propane."

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

          [11] "Propane dehydrogenation reactions proceed via elementary steps that involve CH bond activation and disposal of hydrogen atoms formed in these reactions."
          [12] "The presence of ex- changed Zn cations increases the rate of these hydrogen re- moval steps by introducing portholes for recombinative desorption of H atoms as H2."

          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>

          [7] "Surface organometallic chemistry (SOMC) allows for the generation of well-defined surface species on a variety of supports via grafting of tailored molecular precursors on supports with isolated OH sites.8 Thus, we reasoned that the development of an appropriate molecular precursor would allow for generating well-defined isolated active sites of gallium outside of bulk Ga2O3."
          [8] "A two-step approach, involving both SOMC and the thermolytic molecular precursor approach has previously been implemented to generate isolated surface sites with controlled oxidation state and nuclearity.9 Herein we describe the synthesis, structural characterization of the molecular complex [Ga(OSi(OtBu)3)3(THF)] (1)10 and its utilization as a precursor for generating gallium single-sites on silica."
          [9] "These isolated gallium sites were achieved through grafting of 1 on silica followed by a thermolysis step at 500 C under high vacuum."
          [10] "The presented gallium species display unprecedented catalytic performances, combining high activity, selectivity and stability in the dehydrogenation of propane."

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

[6] "Exchanged Zn cations increase propane conversion turnover rates, hydrogen formation rates, and selectivity to aromatics on H-ZSM5."
          [7] "These metal cations increase propane conversion rates and the selectivity to unsaturated products by increasing the rate of propane and propene dehydrogenation and by avoiding the preferential removal of hydrogen by transfer to hydrocarbon fragments to form light alkanes."
          [8] "In contrast, Berndt et al. (16) showed that CO reacts on Zn/H-ZSM5 (<2 wt% Zn, Si/Al = 23) to produce equimolar amounts of CO2 and H2,suggesting that (ZnOH)+ is present."
          [9] "This study addresses the synthesis of Zn cation-exchanged H-ZSM5 zeolite and the detailed characterization of the structure and location of the Zn species."
          [10] "The presence of Zn species leads to an increase in the rate of H2 formation. The hydrogen (H2) selectivity increases with increasing Zn content (Fig. 3)."
          [11] "Propane dehydrogenation reactions proceed via elementary steps that involve CH bond activation and disposal of hydrogen atoms formed in these reactions."
          [12] "The presence of ex- changed Zn cations increases the rate of these hydrogen re- moval steps by introducing portholes for recombinative desorption of H atoms as H2."

[1] "The demand for propylene has grown significantly over the years, leading to the development of new production methods, including propane dehydrogenation (PDH)."
          [2] "The PDH process is considered one of the most promising propylene production methods compared to methanol-to-olefins, Fischer-Tropsch-to-olefins, etc."
          [3] "Crucial insights into the PDH process include understanding the adsorption of key propyl intermediates on the catalyst surface."
          [4] "The regulation of material structure and reaction performance at the molecular and atomic levels has attracted extensive attention."
          [5] "The PDH reaction can occur on an individual active site, while larger ensembles of active sites induce structure-sensitive side reactions."
          [6] "To improve the PDH process, strategies involving promoter and support effects have been developed."
          [7] "Catalysts based on metals and/or metal oxides with tunable geometric and electronic properties play crucial roles."
          [8] "The use of promoters such as Cu, Fe, Mn, Co, Sn, Ga, In, Zn can enhance dispersion and tailor electronic states."
          [9] "Supports like Al2O3, SiO2, zeolites can regulate the shape of nanostructured particles and metals-support interaction."
          [10] "Reductive treatment can introduce defects like oxygen vacancies, hydroxyl groups, hydrides enhancing catalytic activity."
          [11] "Promoters like Mg can help disperse V2O5 nanoparticles into polymerized VOx, reducing coke formation."
          [12] "Encapsulation of metal promoters through MSI can alter electron states, affecting catalytic performance."
          [13] "Mesoporous materials provide alternatives for accessing more active sites, confining oxide NPs to prevent sintering."
          [14] "Future challenges include designing NCs with well-defined morphologies and active sites, utilizing in situ/operando techniques."
          [15] "Expanding screening to cheaper transition metals and developing scalable synthesis technologies remains a challenge."
          [16] "CL-ODH as an alternative offers potential, but requires development of nontoxic oxygen carriers with high activity and stability."

[1] "The increasing propylene demand combined with the use of alternative feedstocks such as shale gas has amplified the pressure towards propene production and the development of light alkane dehydrogenation processes."
          [2] "While the two principal industrial processes for PDH utilize CrAl2O3 (CATOFIN) and PtSnAl2O3 (Oleflex) supported catalysts, other materials such as gallium-based catalysts are receiving considerable attention as alternative catalysts."
          [3] "Gallium-based zeolites have already been implemented for the conversion of lightweight alkanes to aromatics and H2, a process proposed to involve a tandem dehydrogenation aromatization process."
          [4] "Ga2O3 and related materials have also been investigated as catalysts for alkane conversion, specifically PDH due to the high selectivity for propylene."
          [5] "Several computational and experimental studies have aimed at identifying these active sites,4f, 4h, 4i, 7 which so far remains a topic of debate."
          [6] "Silica-supported gallium species have been recently prepared by electrostatic adsorption methods.7a While showing promising results, the structure of the active sites is unknown."
          [7] "Surface organometallic chemistry (SOMC) allows for the generation of well-defined surface species on a variety of supports via grafting of tailored molecular precursors on supports with isolated OH sites.8 Thus, we reasoned that the development of an appropriate molecular precursor would allow for generating well-defined isolated active sites of gallium outside of bulk Ga2O3."
          [8] "A two-step approach, involving both SOMC and the thermolytic molecular precursor approach has previously been implemented to generate isolated surface sites with controlled oxidation state and nuclearity.9 Herein we describe the synthesis, structural characterization of the molecular complex [Ga(OSi(OtBu)3)3(THF)] (1)10 and its utilization as a precursor for generating gallium single-sites on silica."
          [9] "These isolated gallium sites were achieved through grafting of 1 on silica followed by a thermolysis step at 500 C under high vacuum."
          [10] "The presented gallium species display unprecedented catalytic performances, combining high activity, selectivity and stability in the dehydrogenation of propane."

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>

          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>

          [4] "Ga2O3 and related materials have also been investigated as catalysts for alkane conversion, specifically PDH due to the high selectivity for propylene."
          [5] "Several computational and experimental studies have aimed at identifying these active sites,4f, 4h, 4i, 7 which so far remains a topic of debate."
          [6] "Silica-supported gallium species have been recently prepared by electrostatic adsorption methods.7a While showing promising results, the structure of the active sites is unknown."
          [7] "Surface organometallic chemistry (SOMC) allows for the generation of well-defined surface species on a variety of supports via grafting of tailored molecular precursors on supports with isolated OH sites.8 Thus, we reasoned that the development of an appropriate molecular precursor would allow for generating well-defined isolated active sites of gallium outside of bulk Ga2O3."
          [8] "A two-step approach, involving both SOMC and the thermolytic molecular precursor approach has previously been implemented to generate isolated surface sites with controlled oxidation state and nuclearity.9 Herein we describe the synthesis, structural characterization of the molecular complex [Ga(OSi(OtBu)3)3(THF)] (1)10 and its utilization as a precursor for generating gallium single-sites on silica."
          [9] "These isolated gallium sites were achieved through grafting of 1 on silica followed by a thermolysis step at 500 C under high vacuum."
          [10] "The presented gallium species display unprecedented catalytic performances, combining high activity, selectivity and stability in the dehydrogenation of propane."

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>Herein, a one-step hydrothermal method is employed to synthesize sheet-shaped CoAl2O3HT catalysts for efficiently catalyzing the PDH reaction.</c>

"[1] Among this family of reactions, propane dehydrogenation (PDH) is of particular interest, since propylene is a crucial feedstock for polymer production."
          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>

          "[2] However, improved PDH catalysts are continuously sought."
          "[3] Recently, PDH catalysts involving group IIIA metal oxides have attracted attention."
          "[4] Since each single oxide component exhibited some activity, we hypothesized that the mixed InGa oxide catalysts could show interesting PDH properties different from the two individual oxide catalysts."
          "[5] The resulting mixed-metal oxides exhibit a considerably higher activity in terms of propane conversion than previously reported mixed In2O3Al2O3, as well as compared to -Ga2O3, on both a catalyst mass basis and surface area basis."

<c>For instance, the coordinately unsaturated Al3+ sites present on the (100) facets of commercial c-Al2O3 can serve as anchor sites to anchor atomically dispersed Pt and Ru sites [36,37].</c>
          <c>The specific interaction between Ga2O3 and Al2O3 can allow the tetrahedral Ga3+ cations to highly disperse in the spinel-type c-Ga2O3-Al2O3 solid solution, leading to an enhanced activity and stability in PDH reaction [38].</c>
          <c>The c-Al2O3 nanosheet containing 27% penta-coordinated Al3+ sites has been proved that it could nicely disperse and stabilize bimetallic PtSn nanoclusters because of the strong interactions between metals and support [39].</c>
          <c>This PtSn/Al2O3 sheet catalyst displayed an excellent performance at an ultrahigh space velocity in a long-term PDH reaction.</c>
          <c>In addition to being an appropriate support, the hydroxyl groups-eliminated Al2O3 showed a high activity of coordinately unsaturated Al3+ as the surface active sites in non-oxidative dehydrogenation of isobutane to isobutylene [40].</c>
          <c>Furthermore, the diversity and complexity on the structure of Al2O3, for example the surface acidity at the low-coordinated Al sites, determined the different properties in the adsorption and the activation of propane as well as coke deposition in the PDH reaction.</c>
